Carpino">John Carpino</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Los Angeles Angels</b> are an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> franchise based in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>. The Angels compete in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member club of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) <a href="/wiki/American_League_West" title="American League West">West</a> division. The Angels have played home games at <a href="/wiki/Angel_Stadium" title="Angel Stadium">Angel Stadium</a> since 1966. The current MLB franchise was established as an <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a> in 1961 by  <a href="/wiki/Gene_Autry" title="Gene Autry">Gene Autry</a> (1907-1998), the team\'s first owner. Autry was a famous singing cowboy actor in a series of films in the 1930s to 1950s, and later was the subject of the Gene Autry Western Heritage Museum. The "Angels" name was taken by Autry in tribute to the previous <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_(PCL)" title="Los Angeles Angels (PCL)">original Los Angeles Angels</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League</a> franchise in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_League" title="Pacific Coast League">Pacific Coast League</a> (PCL), which played in <a href="/wiki/South_Los_Angeles" title="South Los Angeles">South Central Los Angeles</a> from 1903 to 1957.  He bought the rights to the Angels name from <a href="/wiki/Walter_O%27Malley" title="Walter O&#39;Malley">Walter O\'Malley</a>, the then-<a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> owner, who acquired the PCL franchise from <a href="/wiki/Philip_K._Wrigley" title="Philip K. Wrigley">Philip K. Wrigley</a>, also the owner of the parent <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> at the time, as part of the Dodgers\' move to Southern California.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctext">Los Angeles Dodgers</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Game_attendance"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Game attendance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Logos_and_colors"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Logos and colors</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Radio_and_television"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Radio and television</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Film_&amp;_TV"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Film &amp; TV</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Season_records"><span class="toctext">Awards and honors</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Retired_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Retired numbers</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#Out_of_circulation,_but_not_retired"><span class="tocnumber">9.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Out of circulation, but not retired</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Angels_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Angels Hall of Fame</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Team_captains"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Team captains</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Baseball_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">Baseball Hall of Fame</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Ford_C._Frick_Award_recipients"><span class="tocnumber">9.4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ford C. Frick Award recipients</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Current_roster"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Current roster</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Minor_league_affiliations"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Minor league affiliations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_history">Franchise history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Franchise history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Los_Angeles_Angels" title="History of the Los Angeles Angels">History of the Los Angeles Angels</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:167px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LAAngels-logo.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/8f/LAAngels-logo.gif" width="165" height="137" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="165" data-file-height="137" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LAAngels-logo.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1963\xe2\x80\x931964. An early logo used by the Los Angeles Angels.</div></div></div>\n<p>The "Los Angeles Angels" name originates from the first Los Angeles-based sports team, the <i>Los Angeles Angels</i>, who took the name "Angels" from the English translation of "Los Angeles", which means "The Angels" in Spanish. The team name started in 1892; in 1903, the team name continued in L.A. through the PCL, which is now a minor league affiliate of <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">MiLB</a>. The Angels franchise of today was established in MLB in 1961 after former owner <a href="/wiki/Gene_Autry" title="Gene Autry">Gene Autry</a> bought the rights to continue the franchise name from Walter O\'Malley, the former <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> owner who had acquired the franchise from <a href="/wiki/Phil_Wrigley" class="mw-redirect" title="Phil Wrigley">Phil Wrigley</a>, the owner of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> at the time. As stated in the book <i>Under the Halo: The Official History of Angels Baseball</i>, "Autry agreed to buy the franchise name for $350,000, and  continue the history of the previously popular Pacific Coast League team as his own expansion team in the MLB."<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>  After the Angels joined the Major Leagues, some players from the Angels\' PCL team joined the Major League Angels in 1961.\n</p><p>As an expansion franchise, the club continued in Los Angeles as the "Los Angeles Angels", and played their home games at Los Angeles\' <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field_(Los_Angeles)" title="Wrigley Field (Los Angeles)">Wrigley Field</a> (not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">stadium of the same name</a>), which had formerly been the home of the PCL <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_(PCL)" title="Los Angeles Angels (PCL)">Los Angeles Angels</a>. The Angels were one of two expansion teams established as a result of the <a href="/wiki/1961_Major_League_Baseball_expansion" title="1961 Major League Baseball expansion">1961 Major League Baseball expansion</a>, along with the second incarnation of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1961%E2%80%9371)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x9371)">Washington Senators</a> (now Texas Rangers). The team then moved in <a href="/wiki/1962_in_baseball" title="1962 in baseball">1962</a> to newly built <a href="/wiki/Dodger_Stadium" title="Dodger Stadium">Dodger Stadium</a>, which the Angels referred to as <a href="/wiki/Chavez_Ravine" title="Chavez Ravine">Chavez Ravine</a>, where they were tenants of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> through <a href="/wiki/1965_in_baseball" title="1965 in baseball">1965</a>.\n</p><p>The team\'s founder, entertainer <a href="/wiki/Gene_Autry" title="Gene Autry">Gene Autry</a>, owned the franchise for its first 36&#160;years. During Autry\'s ownership, the team made the playoffs three times, but never won the pennant. The team has gone through several name changes in their history, first changing their name to the <b>California Angels</b> on September 2, 1965, with a month still left in the season, in recognition of their upcoming move to the newly constructed <a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim Stadium">Anaheim Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim">Anaheim</a> at the start of the 1966 season.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> took control of the team in <a href="/wiki/1997_in_baseball" title="1997 in baseball">1997</a>, it extensively renovated Anaheim Stadium, which was then renamed <a href="/wiki/Edison_International_Field_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Edison International Field of Anaheim">Edison International Field of Anaheim</a>. The City of Anaheim contributed $30&#160;million to the $118&#160;million renovation with a renegotiated lease providing that the names of both the stadium and team contain the word "Anaheim".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The team was renamed the <b>Anaheim Angels</b> and became a subsidiary of Disney Sports, Inc. (later renamed <a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Sports" title="Anaheim Sports">Anaheim Sports, Inc.</a>). Under Disney\'s ownership and the leadership of manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Scioscia" title="Mike Scioscia">Mike Scioscia</a>, the Angels won their first pennant and World Series championship in <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002</a>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/2005_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2005 Major League Baseball season">2005</a>, new owner Arturo Moreno added "Los Angeles" to the team\'s name. In compliance with the terms of its lease with the city of Anaheim, which required "Anaheim" be a part of the team\'s name, the team was renamed the <b>Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</b>. Fans, residents and the municipal governments of both Anaheim and Los Angeles all objected to the change, with the City of Anaheim pursuing litigation; nevertheless, the change <a href="/wiki/City_of_Anaheim_v._Angels_Baseball_LP" title="City of Anaheim v. Angels Baseball LP">was eventually upheld in court</a> and the city dropped its lawsuit in 2009. The team usually refers to itself as the <i>Angels</i> or <i>Angels Baseball</i> in its home media market, and the words "Los Angeles" and "LAA" do not appear in the stadium, on the Angels\' uniforms, or on official team merchandise. Local media in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a> tend to omit a geographic identifier and refer to the team as <i>the Angels</i> or as <i>the Halos.</i> The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>, the most prominent news service in the U.S., refers to the team as <i>the Los Angeles Angels</i>, <i>the Angels</i>, or <i>Los Angeles</i>. The team refers to itself as the "Los Angeles Angels" on its social media accounts, including Twitter, Facebook, and Instagram.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the team was to officially drop "of Anaheim" from its name, as part of a new Angel Stadium lease negotiated with the Anaheim city government.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The deal was never finalized, though as of 2017, most official sources omit the "of Anaheim" suffix and the official MLB Style Guide has referred to the team as simply the <i>Los Angeles Angels</i> since the 2016 season.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_traditions">Team traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Team traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The mantra "Win One for the Cowboy" is a staple that is deeply rooted in Angels history for fans. The saying refers to the Angels\' founder and previous owner, <a href="/wiki/Gene_Autry" title="Gene Autry">Gene Autry</a>, who never saw his Angels win a World Series in his 38&#160;years as owner. Years went by as the team experienced many losses just strikes away from American League pennants. By the Angels\' first World Series Championship in 2002, Autry had died, but after winning the World Series, Angels player Tim Salmon ran into the home dugout and brought out one of Autry\'s signature white Stetson hats in honor of the "singing cowboy". Autry\'s #26 was retired as the 26th man on the field for the Angels.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel Stadium of Anaheim">Angel Stadium of Anaheim</a> is nicknamed "The Big A."<sup id="cite_ref-Angel_Stadium_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angel_Stadium-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> It has a section in center field nicknamed the "California Spectacular", a formation of artificial rocks made to look like a desert mountain in California. The California Spectacular has a running waterfall, and also shoots fireworks from the rocks before every game; anytime the Angels hit a home run or win a game the fireworks shoot from the rocks as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Angel_Stadium_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angel_Stadium-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each game begins with the song "<a href="/wiki/Calling_All_Angels" title="Calling All Angels">Calling All Angels</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Train_(band)" title="Train (band)">Train</a> being played accompanied by a video that shows historical moments in team history, with <a href="/wiki/Norman_Greenbaum" title="Norman Greenbaum">Norman Greenbaum</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Spirit_in_the_Sky" title="Spirit in the Sky">Spirit in the Sky</a>" being played during the team\'s starting lineup announcement.\n</p><p>Anytime the Angels win a game, the saying "Light Up the Halo!", or "Light That Baby Up!" is used in reference to the giant landmark which is a big 230&#160;foot tall A with a halo surrounding the top which lights up every time the Angels win a game.<sup id="cite_ref-Angel_Stadium_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angel_Stadium-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Fans also use the saying, "Just another Halo victory", as the late Angels broadcaster Rory Markas, who would say the catch phrase after each win.\n</p><p>The Angels organization was the first North American team to employ the use of <a href="/wiki/Thundersticks" title="Thundersticks">thundersticks</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Rally_Monkey">The Rally Monkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Rally Monkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rally_Monkey" title="Rally Monkey">Rally Monkey</a> is a mascot for the Angels which appears if the Angels are losing a game or if the game is tied from the 7th inning on, but sometimes earlier depending on the situation. The Rally Monkey appears on the scoreboard in various movies or pop culture references that have been edited to include him.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The Rally Monkey was born in 2000 when the scoreboard showed a clip from <i><a href="/wiki/Ace_Ventura:_Pet_Detective" title="Ace Ventura: Pet Detective">Ace Ventura: Pet Detective</a></i>, after which the Angels rallied to win the game. The clip proved to be so popular that the team hired Katie, a white-haired capuchin monkey, to star in original clips for later games. When seen, she jumps up and down to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Pain" title="House of Pain">House of Pain</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Jump_Around" title="Jump Around">Jump Around</a>" and holds a sign that says "RALLY TIME!"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The Rally Monkey came to national and worldwide attention during the Angels\' appearance in the <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002 World Series</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2002_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2002 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a>. In the 6th game, the Angels were playing at home, but were trailing the series 3-2 and facing elimination. They were down 5-0 as the game entered the bottom of the 7th inning. Amid fervid rally-monkey themed fan support, the Angels proceeded to score six unanswered runs over the next two innings, winning the game and turning the momentum of the series for good (they went on to clinch the championship in game 7).\n</p><p>From 2007 to 2009, the Angels reached the post-season each year, sparking a renewal of the Rally Monkey\'s popularity.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Angels have developed many rivalries in and also outside of their division. They include the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Halos-Yanks_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halos-Yanks-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Angels_Texas_rivalry_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angels_Texas_rivalry-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a>, and the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_Rangers">Texas Rangers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Texas Rangers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Rangers and Angels rivalry has been said to develop over a domination in the division between the two teams, and also in recent years more animosity between the two teams due to the amount of former players from each team playing for the division rival. Players such as <a href="/wiki/Mike_Napoli" title="Mike Napoli">Mike Napoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darren_Oliver" title="Darren Oliver">Darren Oliver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Guerrero" title="Vladimir Guerrero">Vladimir Guerrero</a>, <a href="/wiki/C._J._Wilson" title="C. J. Wilson">C. J. Wilson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hamilton" title="Josh Hamilton">Josh Hamilton</a> have all been acquisitions the two division rivals have made from one another. In 2012, Wilson played a joke on Napoli, his former teammate, by <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeting</a> his phone number, causing Napoli to exchange words with Wilson.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The feuds go back to two incidents between Angels second baseman <a href="/wiki/Adam_Kennedy" title="Adam Kennedy">Adam Kennedy</a> and Rangers catcher <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Laird" title="Gerald Laird">Gerald Laird</a> which led to punches being thrown.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The two teams have each had a perfect game against each other, including <a href="/wiki/Mike_Witt" title="Mike Witt">Mike Witt</a> in 1984 at <a href="/wiki/Arlington_Stadium" title="Arlington Stadium">Arlington Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Rogers_(baseball)" title="Kenny Rogers (baseball)">Kenny Rogers</a> in 1994 at <a href="/wiki/The_Ballpark_in_Arlington" class="mw-redirect" title="The Ballpark in Arlington">The Ballpark in Arlington</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Yankees">New York Yankees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: New York Yankees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Angels and Yankees rivalry can be seen as stemming from heated play between the two teams through the years, including several times in the playoffs. In 1998 there was concern from New York sportswriters that the Angels could upset the Yankees in the Division Series. The Angels missed the playoffs, and the Yankees went on to win later that year. The Angels would knock off the Yankees four years later in the <a href="/wiki/2002_ALDS" class="mw-redirect" title="2002 ALDS">2002 ALDS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Coincidental enough, the former PCL Angels were nicknamed "Yankees West" due to the success the team had, and even held multiple scrimmage games between the two in the old Wrigley Field in Los Angeles during spring training throughout the 30s, 40s, and 50s.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Los_Angeles_Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Los Angeles Dodgers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Freeway_Series" title="Freeway Series">Freeway Series</a></div>\n<p>The rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> has been referred to as the <i>Freeway Series</i> because of the freeway system (mostly via I-5) linking the two teams\' home fields.<sup id="cite_ref-Freeway_series_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freeway_series-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Freeway Series rivalry developed mostly over the two teams sharing similar regions and fans having been split in Los Angeles, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> <a href="/wiki/Cubs%E2%80%93White_Sox_rivalry" title="Cubs\xe2\x80\x93White Sox rivalry">rivalry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/Oakland_A%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland A&#39;s">Oakland A\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Bay_Bridge_Series" title="Bay Bridge Series">rivalry</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> <a href="/wiki/Mets-Yankees_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Mets-Yankees rivalry">rivalry</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_attendance">Game attendance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Game attendance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Angels have drawn more than 3&#160;million fans to the stadium for 16 years straight, and at least 2&#160;million for 17 seasons, and a game average in 2010, 2011, 2012, &amp; 2013 of 40,000 fans at each game despite not making the playoffs all four years.<sup id="cite_ref-angels_stadium_attendance_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-angels_stadium_attendance-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> This is 2nd in all of MLB, only trailing the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. In 2014, the Angels were fifth in the MLB in attendance, with a total of 3,095,935 people.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2015, the Angels fans have set 6 Guinness World Records for the largest gatherings of people wearing blankets, wrestling masks, cowboy hats, wigs, Santa hats, superhero capes, and sombreros. They\'ve also set the world record for largest gathering of people with selfie sticks.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2009, the Angels were voted the number one franchise in professional sports in Fan Value by ESPN magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-fan_value_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fan_value-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, ESPN &amp; Fan polls by ESPN ranked the Angels #4 in the best sports franchises, ahead of every Major League team in baseball at #1 and also making it the #1 sports franchise in Los Angeles. The rankings were determined through a combination of sports analysts and fan votes ranking all sports franchises by a combination of average fan attendance, fan relations, "Bang for your Buck" or winning percentage over the past 3&#160;years, ownership, affordability, stadium experience, players effort on the field and likability, coaching, and "Title Track".\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_colors">Logos and colors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Logos and colors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AnaheimAngels.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/AnaheimAngels.svg/220px-AnaheimAngels.svg.png" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/AnaheimAngels.svg/330px-AnaheimAngels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/AnaheimAngels.svg/440px-AnaheimAngels.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="306" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AnaheimAngels.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2002\xe2\x80\x932004. The second logo under the "Anaheim" name and Disney ownership.</div></div></div><p> The Los Angeles Angels have used ten different logos and three different color combinations throughout their history. Their first two logos depict a baseball with wings and a halo over a baseball diamond with the letters "L" and "A" over it in different styles. The original team colors were the predominantly blue with a red trim. This color scheme would be in effect for most of the franchise\'s history lasting from 1961 to 1996.\n</p><p>On September 2, 1965, with the team still a tenant of the Dodgers at Chavez Ravine, Autry changed its name from the "Los Angeles Angels" to the "California Angels." With the club\'s 1966 move to <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim</a>, the logo changed as well. During the 31&#160;years of being known as the "California Angels", the team kept the previous color scheme, however, their logo did change six times during this period. The first logo under this name was very similar to the previous "LA" logo, the only difference was instead of an interlocking "LA", there was an interlocking "CA." Directly after this from 1971 to 1985, the Angels adopted a logo that had the word "Angels" written on an outline of the State of California. Between the years 1971\xe2\x80\x931972 the "A" was lower-case while from 1973 to 1985 it was upper-case.\n</p><p>It was in 1965, while the stadium was being finished, that Bud Furillo (of the Herald Examiner) coined its nickname, "the Big A" after <a href="/wiki/Big_A_Sign" title="Big A Sign">the tall letter A that once stood beyond left-center field</a> and served as the arena\'s primary scoreboard (it was later relocated to a section of the parking lot, south-east of the stadium).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg/220px-Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg/330px-Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg/440px-Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="565" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Angel_Stadium_of_Anaheim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Angel Stadium of Anaheim</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1986, the Angels adopted the "big A" on top of a baseball as their new logo, with the shadow of California in the background. After the "big A" was done in 1992, the Angels returned to their roots and re-adopted the interlocking "CA" logo with some differences. The Angels used this logo from 1993 to 1996, during that time, the "CA" was either on top of a blue circle or with nothing else.\n</p><p>After the renovations of then-Anaheim Stadium and the takeover by the Walt Disney Company, the Angels changed their name to the "Anaheim Angels" along with changing the logo and color scheme. The first logo under Disney removed the halo and had a rather cartoon-like "ANGELS" script with a wing on the "A" over a periwinkle plate and crossed bats. With this change, the Angels\' color scheme changed to dark blue and periwinkle. After a run with the "winged" logo from 1997 to 2001, Disney changed the Angels\' logo back to a "Big A" with a silver halo over a dark blue baseball diamond. With this logo change, the colors changed to the team\'s current color scheme: predominantly red with some dark blue and white.\n</p><p>When the team\'s name changed from the "Anaheim Angels" to the "Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim", the logo changed only slightly, the name "ANAHEIM ANGELS" and the blue baseball diamond were removed leaving only the "Big A."\n</p><p>For the 2011 season, as part of the 50th anniversary of the Angels franchise, the halo on the \'Big A\' logo temporarily changed colors from silver to old gold, paying tribute to the Angels logos of the past (and also the 50th Anniversary tradition of gold). The uniforms also reflected the change to the gold halo for this season.\n</p><p>During the 50th Anniversary season the players wore throwback jerseys at each Friday home game reflecting all the different logos and uniforms previously worn by players. Also, Angels alumni from past seasons threw the ceremonious first pitch at every home game during the 50th Anniversary season.\n</p><p>A new patch was added on the uniforms before the 2012 season, featuring a red circle encircling the words "Angels Baseball" and the club logo inside and flanking the year 1961 in the middle, which was the year the Angels franchise was established.  With this new patch, the Angels\' A with the halo now appears on three different locations of the jersey - the right shoulder, the wordmark, and the left shoulder.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Angels_broadcasters" title="List of Los Angeles Angels broadcasters">List of Los Angeles Angels broadcasters</a></div>\n<p>As of  2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Angels\' <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> radio station is <a href="/wiki/KLAA_(AM)" title="KLAA (AM)">KLAA</a> 830AM, which is owned by the Angels themselves and <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> It replaces <a href="/wiki/KSPN_(AM)" title="KSPN (AM)">KSPN</a> (710 ESPN), on which frequency had aired most Angels games since the team\'s inception in 1961. That station, then KMPC, aired games from <a href="/wiki/1961_in_baseball" title="1961 in baseball">1961</a> to <a href="/wiki/1996_in_baseball" title="1996 in baseball">1996</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1997_in_baseball" title="1997 in baseball">1997</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/1998_in_baseball" title="1998 in baseball">1998</a>, the flagship station became <a href="/wiki/KRLA" title="KRLA">KRLA</a> (1110AM). In <a href="/wiki/1999_in_baseball" title="1999 in baseball">1999</a>, it was replaced by <a href="/wiki/KLAC" title="KLAC">KLAC</a> for four seasons, including the <a href="/wiki/2002_Anaheim_Angels_season" title="2002 Anaheim Angels season">2002 World Series season</a>.\n</p><p>The Angels 2010 broadcast line-up was thrown into doubt with the death of <a href="/wiki/Rory_Markas" title="Rory Markas">Rory Markas</a> in January 2010. The Angels had announced in November 2009 that Markas and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Gubicza" title="Mark Gubicza">Mark Gubicza</a> would broadcast Angels\' televised games, with <a href="/wiki/Terry_Smith_(radio)" class="mw-redirect" title="Terry Smith (radio)">Terry Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mota_(baseball)" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Mota (baseball)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Mota</a> handling the radio side.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, the Angels announced that <a href="/wiki/Steve_Physioc" title="Steve Physioc">Steve Physioc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rex_Hudler" title="Rex Hudler">Rex Hudler</a> would not return to the broadcasting team. On March 3, 2010 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Victor_Rojas" title="Victor Rojas">Victor Rojas</a> will replace Markas.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, KLAA broadcast spring training games on <a href="/wiki/Tape_delay_(broadcasting)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tape delay (broadcasting)">tape delay</a> from the beginning on February 28 to March 9 because of advertiser commitments to some daytime talk shows. Those games were available live only online. Live preseason broadcasts were to begin on March 10.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009, <a href="/wiki/KFWB_(AM)" class="mw-redirect" title="KFWB (AM)">KFWB</a> 980AM started broadcasting 110 weekday games, including postseason games, to better reach listeners in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles County">Los Angeles County</a> and other areas to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>  All 162&#160;games plus post season games still air on KLAA.\n</p><p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/KSPN_(AM)" title="KSPN (AM)">KSPN</a> 710AM broadcast at least 60 weekday games. This was a partial return to their old station from 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Angels radio broadcasts are also in Spanish on <a href="/wiki/KWKW" title="KWKW">KWKW</a> 1330AM and KWKU 1220AM.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Net_West/Prime_Ticket" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox Sports Net West/Prime Ticket">Fox Sports West</a> holds the exclusive rights to the regional telecasts of approximately 150 Angels home and away games.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Fox owned and operated <a href="/wiki/MyNetworkTV" title="MyNetworkTV">MyNetworkTV</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/KCOP-TV" title="KCOP-TV">KCOP-TV</a> broadcast select games from 2006 to 2011, but opted to move those games to <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_West" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox Sports West">Fox Sports West</a> in 2012. As all MLB teams, select national Angels telecasts can be found on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_TBS" title="Major League Baseball on TBS">TBS</a> or <a href="/wiki/MLB_Network" title="MLB Network">MLB Network</a>. During Disney\'s ownership of the franchise, the company planned to start an ESPN West regional sports network in 1999, which would also carry <a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Mighty_Ducks" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim Mighty Ducks">Anaheim Mighty Ducks</a> ice hockey games, but the plan was abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 2009 season, Physioc and Hudler called about 100&#160;games, while Markas and Gubicza had the remaining game telecasts (about 50, depending on <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Major_League_Baseball" title="ESPN Major League Baseball">ESPN</a> and <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball on Fox">Fox</a> exclusive national schedules). The split arrangement dated back to the 2007 season, when Mota and Gubicza were the second team. Markas debuted on TV in a three-game series at the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> in August 2007.\n</p><p>Mota, who is <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a> and the son of former <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Dodger</a> <a href="/wiki/Manny_Mota" title="Manny Mota">Manny Mota</a>, has also called Angels games in Spanish, and at one time did analysis from the <a href="/wiki/Dugout_(baseball)" title="Dugout (baseball)">dugout</a> rather than the usual booth position.\n</p><p>All locally broadcast games are produced by FSN regardless of the outlet actually showing the games.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dick_Enberg" title="Dick Enberg">Dick Enberg</a>, who broadcast Angels baseball in the 1970s, is the broadcaster most identified with the Angels, using such phrases as "Oh, my!", "Touch \'em all!" after Angel home runs, and "The halo shines tonight!"\n</p><p>Other former Angels broadcasters over the past three decades include <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Blattner" title="Buddy Blattner">Buddy Blattner</a>, Don Wells, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Niehaus" title="Dave Niehaus">Dave Niehaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Starr_(sportscaster)" title="Bob Starr (sportscaster)">Bob Starr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Torre" title="Joe Torre">Joe Torre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Olden" title="Paul Olden">Paul Olden</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Wisk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Wisk (page does not exist)">Al Wisk</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Conin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Conin (page does not exist)">Al Conin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Impemba" title="Mario Impemba">Mario Impemba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sparky_Anderson" title="Sparky Anderson">Sparky Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Reuss" title="Jerry Reuss">Jerry Reuss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Wilson_(sportscaster)" title="Ken Wilson (sportscaster)">Ken Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Brett" title="Ken Brett">Ken Brett</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Fairly" title="Ron Fairly">Ron Fairly</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Coleman" title="Jerry Coleman">Jerry Coleman</a> also spent time with the Angels organization in the early 1970s as a pre-game and post-game host before joining the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> broadcast team.\n</p><p>From 1994 until the end of the 2012 season, the <a href="/wiki/Public_address_announcer" class="mw-redirect" title="Public address announcer">public address announcer</a> for most Angels home games was <a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Courtney_(announcer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="David Courtney (announcer) (page does not exist)">David Courtney</a>, who also served as the public address announcer for the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings" title="Los Angeles Kings">Los Angeles Kings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers" title="Los Angeles Clippers">Los Angeles Clippers</a> and a traffic reporter for Angels flagship KLAA 830&#160;AM until his death on November 29, 2012,.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Starting in the 2013 season, Michael Araujo, the PA Announcer for the <a href="/wiki/LA_Galaxy" title="LA Galaxy">LA Galaxy</a> since 2002, was selected as the new public address announcer for the Angels.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>  Anaheim Ducks announcer Phil Hulett serves as the secondary public address announcer.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Film_.26_TV"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_&amp;_TV">Film &amp; TV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Film &amp; TV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> remade the 1951 film <i><a href="/wiki/Angels_in_the_Outfield_(1951_film)" title="Angels in the Outfield (1951 film)">Angels in the Outfield</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Angels_in_the_Outfield_(1994_film)" title="Angels in the Outfield (1994 film)">1994</a> with the California Angels as the team that receives heavenly assistance.</li>\n<li>The team is also featured in the 1988 comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Naked_Gun" title="The Naked Gun">The Naked Gun</a></i>.</li>\n<li>The 1990 comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Taking_Care_of_Business_(film)" title="Taking Care of Business (film)">Taking Care of Business</a></i> features a world series matchup between the Chicago Cubs and the California Angels.</li>\n<li>The 1991 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Talent_for_the_Game" title="Talent for the Game">Talent for the Game</a></i> features <a href="/wiki/Edward_James_Olmos" title="Edward James Olmos">Edward James Olmos</a> as a baseball scout for the California Angels.</li>\n<li>During Disney\'s ownership of the Angels, the team was also featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Air_Bud:_Seventh_Inning_Fetch" title="Air Bud: Seventh Inning Fetch">Air Bud: Seventh Inning Fetch</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Deuce_Bigalow:_Male_Gigolo" title="Deuce Bigalow: Male Gigolo">Deuce Bigalow: Male Gigolo</a></i>, and TV movie <i><a href="/wiki/Angels_in_the_Infield" title="Angels in the Infield">Angels in the Infield</a></i>.</li>\n<li>Most recently, the Angels and Angel Stadium were featured in <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory_(season_8)" title="The Big Bang Theory (season 8)">season 8</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory" title="The Big Bang Theory">The Big Bang Theory</a></i> in an episode titled "The First Pitch Insufficiency".</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_records">Season records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Angels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Season records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Angels_seasons" title="List of Los Angeles Angels seasons">List of Los Angeles Angels seasons</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Angeles Angels award winners and league leaders">Los Angeles Angels award winners and league leaders</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span 1997</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a 1997 to honor Jackie Robinson.</li></ul>\n<h4><span id="Out_of_circulation.2C_but_not_retired"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Out_of_circulation,_but_not_retired">Out of circulation, but not Salmon</a>\'s retirement at the end of the 2006 season</li>\n<li>No. 34 has been out of circulation since <a href="/wiki/Nick_Adenhart" title="Nick Adenhart">Nick Adenhart</a>\'s untimely death in
